# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

**Sourcegraph Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/node--v22.13.0`

# Node.js child_process Command Injection Guards

## Your Task

Find all JavaScript and C++ source files in nodejs/node that implement input validation and command injection prevention for the child_process module. Identify: the normalizeSpawnArguments function with null-byte validation, the exec/execFile/spawn entry points, the internal ChildProcess class that interfaces with C++, the ProcessWrap native binding, and the validator functions (validateArgumentNullCheck) used to prevent injection.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/node--v22.13.0.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/node--v22.13.0` (nodejs/node)

## Key Findings

### **Validation Functions (lib/child_process.js)**
1. **`validateArgumentNullCheck()`** (lines 963-967) - Checks individual string arguments for null bytes
2. **`validateArgumentsNullCheck()`** (lines 970-974) - Validates arrays of arguments

### **Normalization Functions (lib/child_process.js)**
1. **`normalizeSpawnArguments()`** (lines 538-709) - Comprehensive validation for spawn parameters
2. **`normalizeExecArgs()`** (lines 188-206) - Validates command strings for exec
3. **`normalizeExecFileArgs()`** (lines 262-296) - Validates execFile parameters

### **Public API Entry Points (lib/child_process.js)**
All six methods enforce null-byte validation:
- `exec()` (line 231)
- `execSync()` (line 945)
- `execFile()` (line 323)
- `execFileSync()` (line 907)
- `spawn()` (line 745)
- `spawnSync()` (line 823)
- `fork()` (line 122)

### **JavaScript-to-C++ Interface (lib/internal/child_process.js)**
- **`ChildProcess`** class (lines 254-311) - Wraps native Process handle and interfaces with C++

### **C++ Native Binding (src/process_wrap.cc)**
- **`ProcessWrap`** class (lines 51-346) - Native binding that handles actual OS process spawning

It throws ERR_INVALID_ARG_VALUE if a null byte is found: 'must be a string without null bytes'.\n\n**validateArgumentsNullCheck()** (lib/child_process.js:970-974) iterates through arrays of arguments (like command arguments or execArgv) and calls validateArgumentNullCheck() on each element to prevent null byte injection in argument arrays.\n\n## Normalization Functions\n\nThree key normalization functions enforce validation across the API:\n\n**normalizeSpawnArguments()** (lib/child_process.js:538-709) normalizes and validates spawn arguments. commands.\n\n**normalizeExecFileArgs()** (lib/child_process.js:262-296) validates argv0 with validateArgumentNullCheck() (line 292) to prevent null byte injection in custom process names.\n\n## Public API Entry Points\n\nAll six main child_process methods use these validation functions:\n\n**exec()** (lib/child_process.js:231-236) calls normalizeExecArgs() which validates the command string against null bytes.\n\n**execSync()** (lib/child_process.js:945-960) uses normalizeExecArgs() for validation before synchronous execution.\n\n**execFile()** (lib/child_process.js:323-522) calls bytes.\n\n**spawnSync()** (lib/child_process.js:823-869) calls normalizeSpawnArguments() to validate all parameters before synchronous process spawning.\n\n**fork()** (lib/child_process.js:122-172) validates execPath with validateArgumentNullCheck() (line 142) and execArgv with validateArgumentsNullCheck() (line 146) to prevent null byte injection in forked processes.\n\n## JavaScript to C++ It:\n- Creates a native Process object via internalBinding('process_wrap') (line 44 imports Process, line 266 creates the handle)\n- Implements ChildProcess.prototype.spawn() (line 354+) which invokes the native spawn method\n- Calls this._handle.spawn(options) (line 395) to pass validated options to C++\n\n## C++ Native Binding\n\n**ProcessWrap** (src/process_wrap.cc:51-346) is the C++ class that implements native process management:\n- Inherits from HandleWrap and provides the native Process binding\n- Exports Initialize() (line 53-69) which sets up the Process constructor and methods\n- Implements Spawn() (line 153-310) which:\n  - Receives already-validated options from JavaScript\n  - Extracts file path, arguments, environment, and stdio configuration\n  - Calls uv_spawn() (line 286) to perform actual OS process spawning\n  - Returns error codes to JavaScript layer\n\nThe validation happens entirely at the JavaScript layer before reaching C++, providing defense-in-depth protection.\n\n## Comprehensive Test Coverage\n\ntest/parallel/test-child-process-reject-null-bytes.js (295 lines) provides regression tests for null byte validation covering:\n- Command string validation (exec, execSync) lines 19-37\n- File path validation (spawn, execFile, execFileSync, spawnSync, fork) lines 40-71\n- Arguments array validation (execFile, execFileSync, fork, spawn, spawnSync) lines 78-101\n- Current working directory validation (lines 104-138)\n- argv0 parameter validation (lines 140-175)\n- Shell parameter validation (lines 177-210)\n- Environment variable keys and values validation (lines 212-282)\n- execPath and execArgv validation for fork (lines 284-294)\n\nAll tests verify that ERR_INVALID_ARG_VALUE TypeError is thrown when null bytes are detected, preventing command injection attacks via string concatenation or argument manipulation."
